## **174: Moving Between Cities and the First Princess**

**AN:** I had planned to split the Crimson Empire arc into a front and back half because I couldn’t seem to finish writing it, but it looks like I’ll manage to wrap it up after all. So I’ve decided to end it within Volume 12 alone.

As a result, it did end up a bit longer.

---

Excluding the goblins who became the noble sacrifices of the “Heroic Spirit Blade: Incomplete”, we reached the city on the sixth layer without encountering any wild monsters.

There were other cities along the way on the seventh layer as well, but due to time constraints we judged there was no need to stop by them.

Rouge said greetings would be a hassle anyway, so the timing worked out nicely.

“It does look like there are fewer spies.”

I’d heard that it was difficult for outsiders to move up layers, in other words, social rank, but it didn’t seem to be impossible. Compared to the seventh layer, the number of spies was practically zero, though not literally zero.

“So there are still some, huh…”

“Well, that just means they’re gutsy spies.”

Rouge’s face twitched at this unknown truth.

When it comes to your own country’s spy situation, it’s better for your mental health not to know too much.

Rouge and her group immediately headed to see the local lord, while we went sightseeing.

Even if the layer changes, the overall character of the country doesn’t change that much.

We enjoyed a townscape similar to ‘Tokiwa City’.

By the way, this city is called ‘Yamabuki City’. I’m not even going to comment on that anymore.

And the first place we headed to was a clothing shop.

“Ta-da! China dresses with makeup!”

Saying that, Mio emerged from the changing room wearing a red child-sized china dress.

“I’ve never had an opportunity to wear something like this before, so it’s a little embarrassing…”

Sakura was blushing too, but she was properly wearing a yellow china dress.

Given Sakura’s past, I can’t imagine she ever had a chance to wear a china dress. Even ordinary people hardly ever wear one…

“It’s easy to move in, but if I move too much it feels like my underwear might show.”

《I don’t caaaare.》

Maria was in green, Dora in blue, both wearing child-sized dresses.

Dora, you should care.

“Doesn’t it show your body lines a bit too much?”

Sera was wearing a white china dress, but she was on a completely different level from the others.

To put it bluntly…

“Sexy.”

“Very sexy.”

“P-please don’t say things like that!”

Dora, Mio, and Maria were wholesome, Sakura was average for better or worse.

Only Sera clearly stood out. In a sexy way.

Of course, to the average Japanese person, a china dress is inherently sexy (prejudice), so in that sense it’s not exactly wrong.

“Maybe something with more ornate embroidery would have been better? Sexy and gorgeous blonde hair really makes a strong character, you know. Then give her an iron fan or something and style her hair in drill curls…”

“She sounds like a game character.”

It seems I pressed a strange switch in Mio, because she started seriously considering it.

What she was wearing now was a basic, simple design.

If we had a sample, the sewing maids could make something even more amazing…

“For now, it’s fine to buy what they’re wearing, right?”

“Ah, yeah. The sizes are fine, so I’ll just pay as is.”

“I personally think there’s a problem…”

Mio spoke to the nearby clerk and paid.

Since they were china dresses, we’d already decided back in ‘Tokiwa City’ that we’d buy them.

However, there weren’t any shops selling china dresses in ‘Tokiwa City’, so we put it off. If tourism were a focus it might be different, but otherwise there’s no reason to stock clothes that don’t sell well. It can’t be helped.

“I feel calmer in my usual clothes.”

“Me too…”

After that, the women changed back into their regular outfits.

This wasn’t because Sakura and Sera had given up, but because wearing them would make them stand out unnecessarily. To begin with, china dresses aren’t everyday wear even for citizens of the Crimson Empire.

And for dinner, we had ramen. With rice on the side.

“Wait, is ramen actually Chinese food?”

“Master, that discussion gets complicated, so let’s stop. For now, it’s confirmed that the people who came to this country were Japanese.”

“No matter how you look at it, the seasoning is aimed at Japanese tastes.”

“Yes, it’s delicious…”

《So gooood.》

At the very least, it’s confirmed that this culture was transmitted by Japanese people.

Well, I’d already been almost certain for quite a while…

“The variety of dishes from Master’s world is amazing.”

“Our country in particular is incredible. If you look for them, you can usually eat delicious food from all over the world. Though they’re often heavily adapted to Japanese tastes…”

“That famous magical modification, huh.”

Apparently, sometimes they’re even said to be better than the original?

Though they end up being recognized as a different dish.

“In that sense, it’s a good thing that the people who got transferred to another world were Japanese.”

Even though it’s another world, if you look around you can find familiar things everywhere.

“If people had been transferred from all over the world, the culture would have been a complete mess.”

“Yeah, being transferred to another world is hard enough, and if the language is Japanese on top of that, anyone from another country would be at a massive disadvantage…”

Being isekai’d is already harsh, and adding a language barrier makes it even worse.

“That’s one of this world’s mysteries, too. Hero summoning seems to be limited to Japan. And I don’t think there’s any information left about other transferees.”

Oh right, if you’re transferred outside of hero summoning, you can die if you’re unlucky.

In that case, there wouldn’t be any information left about foreigners who got transferred.

“Reincarnators also seem to be limited to Japanese so far.”

Well, even if we know that transfers and reincarnations only originate from Japan, it doesn’t really change anything.

“That’s true. Oh, and we might get one more sample in this country.”

Mio calling the emperor of a nation a “sample” really shows how gutsy she is.

Though it might just be that her senses are dulled from spending time with me…

And so, we continued through the cities on the fifth and fourth layers.

Overall, none of the cities were drastically different, and we enjoyed sightseeing well enough.

When we got tired of Chinese food, we’d secretly return to the mansion via ‘Portal’ and eat the maids’ cooking.

Sometimes the flavors are just too strong and you get tired of them.

Everything was going smoothly, but if there was one problem…

“\<Fear>.”

“Ugh, a-ahhh…”

About every other time, the local lord comes out and we end up having to show our strength.

I’m only using \<Fear>, though…

And it looks like we’ll arrive at the city on the third layer today.

“Ugh…”

In the carriage, Rouge made a complicated expression.

“What’s wrong? Did you find something interesting?”

“Why does this look like the face of someone who found something interesting? No, I was looking at the map and saw a familiar name. This.”

“Let me see.”

It seems that person is in the city we’re going to next.

This one.

Name: Carmine Crimson  

Gender: Female  

Age: 17  

Race: Human  

Title: Princess of the Crimson Empire

“So, your niece?”

“Yes, my niece. My brother Scarlet’s second child, his eldest daughter.”

Scarlet’s daughter, apparently.

“Huh? Wasn’t Strawberry the second princess and also seventeen?”

If my memory’s right.

A: Correct.

The timeline doesn’t line up?

“From the first child, it goes eldest son Red, eldest daughter Carmine, second daughter Strawberry. Those three are the same age, half-siblings.”

“Scarlet is… impressive in many ways.”

Not Irish twins, but half-siblings of the same age. He gets around.

“So why did you make that face earlier?”

“Please don’t call it a strange face… Carmine has disliked me since we were young, and she would pick fights with me over anything. Of course, I didn’t just take it lying down.”

“Minerva, was there anything heartwarming about that?”

I ask Minerva to confirm.

You know, from just one perspective it’s hard to tell if it’s something like tsundere behavior.

“No. She genuinely seemed hostile. Honestly, I don’t know the reason.”

“It’s been that way since we were old enough to remember. If there is a reason, it’s something that goes way back.”

If even Minerva doesn’t know, then it’s not something others (outsiders) can easily grasp.

“So is it fine to just go to the city like this?”

“Of course. If we avoid the city, it would look like I’m running from Carmine. I’ve done nothing shameful toward her. There’s no reason to avoid her.”

“You sound just like Master.”

Sera, who’d been listening, cut in.

“Yes, I thought the same as I was saying it. Do slaves take after their masters?”

“I’ve never heard of that.”

“Well, if you hear your master’s words and actions often, it wouldn’t be strange for them to influence you, but Rouge-san, you don’t interact with Master that much, do you?”

“If there’s anyone influenced by Jin-sama, it would be us.”

The slave group denies Rouge’s theory.

“That’s true. Come to think of it, I might have always thought like this.”

Yeah, with Rouge, it’s probably just her original nature.

“Still, if we go greet the local lord, we’ll end up meeting her whether we like it or not. How troublesome…”

Not running away and something being troublesome are two separate issues.

“So what kind of girl is this Princess Carmine?”

“Well… she’s proud, strict with herself and others. Put negatively, she’s arrogant. And even four years ago, she should have already had considerable combat ability.”

“In terms of pure combat power, she’s said to be one of the top two among the emperor’s children.”

Rouge answers Mio’s question, and Minerva adds to it.

“The one she’s competing with for top two is Strawberry.”

“Power Strawberry, Skill Carmine is a well-known nickname pairing.”

“That phrase sounds familiar…”

Just from the nicknames, you can tell their general direction, which is nice.

“What about the eldest son, Red?”

I was a bit curious.

He’s the eldest son, yet not part of the top two?

“Red-sama …doesn’t seem to like fighting very much, so his true strength is unknown.”

“I’ve never seen Red fight either.”

“I kind of had this image that the Crimson Empire’s royalty were all hot-blooded, but I guess not everyone is like that.”

Crimson, blood…

“Why did you get that image? I believe I explained that there are researchers as well…”

“Given the average of the people we’ve met so far, can you blame me?”

“Mmm… I can’t deny it, which is sad.”

Early Rouge, the Scarlet who rampages in other countries, and the power-based Strawberry are all pretty muscle-brained and bloodthirsty.

“Anyway, it didn’t look like Red neglected his training entirely, so he can probably fight to some extent. But in the end, this is all information from four years ago…”

“Whether he really can’t fight, or can but hides his strength…”

If we meet him, I’ll just peek at his status.

And then, the third-layer city, ‘Ochiba City’, came into view.

It feels like the color of the cities is gradually getting closer to red.

“Why is she waiting at the entrance…?”

Rouge mutters with genuine displeasure.

That Carmine person is waiting at the city gate.

“Our advance party stopped by this city, so she found out through the lord. A lookout spotted our carriage from atop the outer wall and reported it.”

“So unnecessary…”

The lookout on the wall that surrounds the city spotted us and told Carmine.

In other words, Carmine was fully intent on an ambush.

“Should we just camp out around here?”

I suggest it on a whim.

“That’s… actually a good idea. I don’t want Carmine to take the initiative.”

It got accepted.

So we set up camp a little off the road and began preparing to spend the night.

I hate to say it, but we have food made by the maids stored in \<Infinite Storage>, plus a safe and clean Room. We also have night watch stronger than the city walls. Whether we camp outside or stay in the city doesn’t make much difference.

Inside a privacy curtain, we set up a table and eat freshly made dinner, delivered straight from the mansion.

“Master, are you getting tired of the Crimson Empire’s cities?”

“I won’t deny it. It’s a country without much variation at the city level. Seeing two or three places is probably enough.”

I answer Mio’s question affirmatively.

Saying “I’m tired” might be too much, but since it’s a class-based society that doesn’t consider tourism, there’s a limit to how much you can enjoy.

“If you were really enjoying sightseeing, you wouldn’t stay outside the city like this.”

“That’s true. …Rouge, isn’t there anything interesting around here?”

I ask Rouge, who’s slurping udon.

“Mmph! Let’s see. Honestly, I don’t think there’s anything around here that would interest Jin-sama. Other than the city, there should only be an abandoned mine.”

“An abandoned mine… I definitely want to check that out.”

“Why!?”

Rouge can’t understand.

Even though mining should be over, abandoned mines are fields where events often happen in games.

Abandoned schools, abandoned ports, anything with ‘abandoned’ usually has events (other example: abandoned villages).

“I kind of get what Master is saying. But isn’t it dangerous?”

“I don’t want Jin-sama to do anything dangerous.”

Maria chimes in after Mio.

“Then should we take a canary with us?”

Apparently, you send a canary ahead to check for harmful substances, since their lethal dose is lower than humans.

And if the canary dies, you run away at full speed.

“Isn’t that cruel?”

“Then we’ll send a harpy instead.”

“I’ll say it again. Isn’t that cruel?”

Harpy is out too.

Later, I asked Chocolat, the Harpy Queen, and apparently the harpies sensed some mysterious unease at that time. They have pretty good instincts.

“It can’t be helped. Then this is exactly when a familiar like El should be used.”

L: Me!? Well, if you tell me to do it, I will…

El isn’t strictly a living being, so it’s not ‘cruel’. Perfect.

“So anyway, we’ll just check the map for poisons, okay? What we really need to watch out for are things like unstable footing and cave-ins.”

“That’s also solved by sending El ahead.”

“Ah… that way of thinking works too…”

Since El’s body is temporary, it can be set not to feel pain.

In terms of handling danger, it’s actually a correct use of a familiar.

“You really are planning to go to the abandoned mine. I doubt there’s anything there…”

Rouge looks a bit exasperated.

“Do you really think there’s nothing at a place I want to go?”

“Ugh… what is this inexplicable persuasiveness…”

There is absolutely something there (guaranteed).

After we finished eating and some time passed, Carmine actually left the city and approached our camp.

According to Alta, she couldn’t stand it anymore.

“Rouge, what do you want to do?”

“Well, if she’s coming to us, there’s no problem. She doesn’t seem to have any guards with her. It’s not dangerous to meet her. If anything, it’s more dangerous for her.”

If she’s coming alone into enemy territory (sort of), then we can just meet her.

So, to make things easier to talk, Rouge and I go out to meet Carmine.

“Why aren’t you entering the city!?”

That was Carmine’s first line after grabbing one of Rouge’s attendants outside and entering the camp. Naturally, she’s addressing Rouge.

Compared to the princesses we’ve met so far, her way of speaking is rougher, more casual. She lacks any princess-like refinement.

“That’s quite the greeting for a relative you haven’t seen in a while, Carmine. As for the answer to your question, it’s because you were lying in wait. I don’t want to go where you’re waiting.”

Rouge is sitting on a chair and acting refined.

“What!? How did you know I was here!? Answer me!”

“I’m not so idle that I’d bother explaining things to a rude little girl.”

“You’re really irritating! That’s why, you old hag-“

“Hey, I told you to stop calling me an old hag. Call me big sister.”

Rouge stands up from her chair to protest.

Her earlier composure is gone.

“I refuse. I’m the eldest daughter, so even if I have brothers, I don’t have an older sister. I don’t need to call anyone ‘big sister’. To me, you’re unquestionably my aunt! And a useless old hag at that!”

“Ggh…”

I’d heard they didn’t get along, but this is pretty bad.

“So why did you come back to the Empire? To make excuses for failing Father’s order? I heard you failed to conquer the Estea Labyrinth and some unrelated people beat you to it. What happened to ‘fastest ever to reach floor 30′? You got overtaken so easily. You really are useless.”

Carmine mocks Rouge provocatively, but knowing the truth, it’s not really provoking.

That unrelated labyrinth ruler would be Shindo Jin.

“The labyrinth? I don’t care about that. I came back because there’s something I must report to my brother with top priority.”

“What is it? Answer me.”

“I have no intention of answering. It’s not something someone like you needs to know.”

“You’re really mocking me…”

Carmine’s anger gauge rises.

“You’re mocking me just the same, Carmine. If you just came to complain about me not entering the city, then go home.”

“No way. This is the perfect opportunity to loudly ridicule the useless, returned old maid!”

I thought it was just her rough way of speaking, but her mouth is seriously foul.

“You really do have a terrible mouth and personality.”

“My personality is better than yours was four years ago. Don’t you know your reputation in the country?”

“Ggh…”

Apparently, Rouge had a bad reputation.

“I’m a unit commander in the Imperial Army now, you know? I’ve got plenty of achievements, and my reputation among the people is leagues better than yours.”

“Grr…”

Carmine boasts confidently, puffing out her chest, while Rouge groans in frustration.

Her chest is… decent. It’s obvious because she’s puffing it out.

Carmine is wearing a women’s military uniform.

As royalty, it’s a bit more ornate, but the basics aren’t that different from a regular soldier’s.

She’s probably in charge of the regular troops stationed in ‘Ochiba City’.

There seem to be many high-level soldiers, so maybe it’s a monster extermination unit?

A: Correct.

According to Minerva, monster extermination units are respected in any city within the country.

“And unlike you, who can’t even use honorifics, I can naturally use polite speech and also speak like a proper lady. Of course, I have no intention of using polite speech with someone like you.”

“D-don’t mock me! I can use polite speech too!”

Rouge retorts. She learned polite speech relatively recently.

“Huh? You couldn’t use polite speech until that age, and now you suddenly can? That’s hard to believe.”

Carmine clearly doesn’t believe Rouge.

Which is understandable.

“Well, I’m not that interested anyway. The point is, I surpass you in every way now. Popularity, status, intelligence, strength, all of it. Are you frustrated? Come on, aren’t you frustrated?”

Carmine relentlessly provokes her.

“…Hmph, you talk big. But there’s one thing you’re wrong about. Whatever else, there’s no way you surpass me in strength. I’ve gained power in the labyrinth too.”

“Oh? Then want to test it?”

“Fine. I’ll show you my power.”

Rouge and Carmine glare sparks at each other.

Both reaching for their weapons…

“Stop. If you’re going to fight, do it outside.”

I stop them.

I’m not saying ‘don’t fight’, but it would be a huge nuisance here.

“Mmm, that’s true…”

“…I’ve been wondering for a while now, but who are you? Ordering me, a princess of this country, around. You’re prepared for the consequences, right?”

Rouge accepts it and puts away her weapon, but Carmine doesn’t back down.

“Carmine, stop it. He is my guard and my guest. I will not tolerate rudeness toward him.”

“A guard and a guest? That makes no sense. …Ah, well, there aren’t that many reasons for a woman to bring a man back to her homeland. Getting caught up with such a dull-looking man, you really are a disgrace to the royal family.”

Carmine’s provocation continues.

Hey now, I won’t tolerate being treated as Rouge’s lover either (that’s cruel in its own way).

As for being ‘dull-looking’ I don’t really care.

“Ggh!? Killing intent!?”

Carmine groans, reaching for her weapon and looking around.

Maria, who had been waiting in another room, released her killing intent.

I don’t mind, but Maria apparently couldn’t forgive the ‘dull-looking’ remark.

“Ugh, what is this pressure!?”

That killing intent becomes almost physical pressure, assaulting only Carmine.

“Ggh… cough, cough…”

It seems she exceeded her tolerance, as Carmine drops to her knees.

She’s struggling to breathe.

Maria has really grown, being able to suppress someone with just killing intent… (deeply moved).

《Maria, stop now.》

《Yes, understood.》

When I send Maria a telepathic message, the killing intent immediately stops.

Carmine collapses on the spot.

“Hah… hah… what… was that…”

“That’s why I told you to stop. Honestly, if you’re going to claim to be my brother’s successor, shouldn’t you work on your ability to judge others? Though I’m not really one to talk.”

She’s right. Especially that last part.

“Rest until you can stand, then go home. Don’t say anything unnecessary, just keep quiet.”

“So arrogant… I haven’t lost yet… I won’t lose to someone like you!”

Carmine tries to stand, but she’s clearly exhausted, and barely manages to raise her upper body.

“With that pathetic state, you want to fight me?”

“Y-yes!”

It’s obviously bravado, but she can’t show weakness in front of Rouge.

“Fine. Then I’ll take you on outside.”

“H-hey!? Let go!”

Remembering my words, Rouge drags Carmine, who can’t stand, out of the camp by her clothes.

“I won.”

A few minutes later, Rouge returns, happily reporting.

Well, I knew already from the map…

“You’re happy about beating someone in that state?”

“In terms of pure strength, no. But thinking of it as getting one over on that annoying Carmine makes me incredibly happy.”

Naturally, Rouge’s fight with Carmine could hardly be called a fight.

Carmine returning to ‘Ochiba City’ in tatters was, by all accounts, a pitiful sight.

## **175: Abandoned Mine Exploration and Miasma**

**AN:** This is a postscript to the previous chapter, but Jonathan is a type of apple. He has siblings from the same mother.

Ash is not a name tied to red. Of course, there is a reason (in a sense, a spoiler).

---

The day after we drove off Carmine, we headed for the abandoned mine, which was recommended as a sightseeing spot.

‘Ochiba City’? Oh, we completely skipped it. The reason is that the (probably) main event, Carmine’s appearance, already ended outside the city.

“Huh. Even though it’s called an abandoned mine, it’s not like the resources ran out?”

“Indeed. This is only something I’ve heard, but apparently it wasn’t abandoned because the resources were depleted. It seems it stopped functioning as a mine for some other reason.”

According to Rouge, the abandoned mine we were heading to had been used as a working mine up until ten years ago, but for some reason, it was suddenly abandoned one day.

Having heard that much, do you really think nothing is going to happen?

The abandoned mine is already displayed on the map, but to avoid spoilers, I haven’t looked at it.

The fact that Alta isn’t saying anything probably means the danger level is low. Of course, that doesn’t mean it’s zero.

After riding in the carriage for several hours, we arrived at the abandoned mine.

“I see. This is pretty bad.”

《Kyaa, it stinks!》

Just from the state of things at the entrance, I could already guess why it had been abandoned.

An overwhelming amount of miasma was swirling there.

Miasma is stagnated magical power.

Magical power permeates the atmosphere, but to varying degrees, it stagnates.

Generally, when that stagnation grows large and becomes like black smoke, it is called miasma.

There are several patterns of miasma, but which one does this fall under?

A: This miasma is-

…Ah, Alta. You don’t have to answer.

I’ll go see it myself.

A: Understood.

“Our statuses are high, and we have Poison Resistance, so it’s not a problem for us, but it looks like it would have a serious negative effect on ordinary people.”

“Yeah, they’d have no choice but to retreat. In a way, it’s like poisonous gas erupting.”

Mio seems convinced by the current state of the abandoned mine.

“Canary…”

“Stop that.”

“Harpy…”

“Stop that too.”

“El…”

“…”

L: Stop for me too, I beg you!

Since Mio didn’t stop the familiar, I summoned El.

“So I really was summoned… But since I was summoned, I’ll do my best!”

“Jin-sama, if you intend to enter the abandoned mine, please stay within the barrier I create.”

“Yeah, I’ll do that.”

Maria’s \<Barrier Arts> are also effective as a countermeasure against miasma.

“Miasma doesn’t affect me, so that’s fine, but being alone is a little lonely…”

El ends up going ahead alone, outside the barrier, and she looks a bit lonely.

“What about Rouge and the others?”

“Having come this far, there is no option but to follow.”

“If Rouge-sama is going, there is no way we would not accompany her.”

The others nod at Minerva’s words.

It seems Rouge’s entire group will be coming along. They really are as close as ever.

Just in case, we sent the horses back to the estate, put the carriage into \<Infinite Storage>, and started exploring the abandoned mine.

Basically, in areas where miasma is dense, no one enters except monsters that have strong resistance to miasma.

Also, when monsters are born from miasma, those born are inherently resistant to miasma.

“In other words, these guys are monsters that are strong against miasma.”

“Just as they appear.”

I mutter as I look at the monster (corpse) before us.

It looks like a pitch-black lizard.

Evil Gecko  

LV30  

\<Miasma Proliferation LV1>  

Notes: A reptilian monster that operates within miasma and gradually expands the area of miasma.

Rather than just being resistant to miasma, it’s specialized in it.

I’m debating whether or not to comment on the name…

Right now, I’ve adjusted the map settings so that only areas we’ve visually confirmed are displayed.

Simply put, like in many games, only “places we’ve already passed through” and “what we can currently see” are shown on the map.

Therefore, I don’t know the total number.

However, we haven’t even walked ten minutes yet, and we’ve already encountered them more than five times.

El, who is clearing the way, is instantly killing them with tail attacks, but…

“Taking out weak monsters one by one is a pain. I want to wipe them out with my breath.”

“No, breathing fire in a mine is something only an absolute idiot would do.”

That would be suicide, plain and simple.

“With this barrier, I think it would endure even a fairly large explosion.”

“That may be true, but still…”

It blocks poison. It lets air through. It doesn’t let shockwaves through.

Isn’t that a bit too convenient?

“Even without the barrier, I think half the members would be fine even if there was an explosion.”

“In that case, the likelihood of us dying would be high.”

Leaving aside the main party, Rouge’s group might have a hard time.

“Got it!”

There was another Evil Gecko, so El tail-attacked it. The opponent dies.

Are only Evil Geckos appearing here?

“They’re so weak, there’s no challenge at all…”

“We’ve inflated quite a bit ourselves. But even without skills, level 30 would be a formidable opponent for ordinary people. It’s no wonder it became abandoned.”

Listening to El complain, Mio mutters.

“In adventurer terms, would that be around C-rank or B-rank territory? At the very least, it’s not something ordinary miners could handle. Even if they’re muscular, levels don’t go up easily unless you defeat monsters…”

This is one of the warped aspects of this world.

Rather than personal training, defeating monsters and gaining experience to level up is a much more efficient way to grow stronger through stat increases. Strength training isn’t completely useless, but the efficiency difference is enormous.

It’s a mysterious principle, almost like a game.

“But a military force could probably handle it, right?”

“There’s no adventurers’ guild, but in exchange, the soldiers were quite strong.”

As Mio and Sera say, it’s true that this country’s military could suppress these monsters.

But they probably haven’t come here. There are far too many monsters for this to be the result of regular extermination.

They’re sweeping monsters elsewhere, yet leaving these ones alone, so there must be some special reason. Maybe we’ll find out as we go deeper?

“Got it!”

Another Evil Gecko appears, and El defeats it with a tail attack.

“No, wait a second.”

Looking closely at the defeated monster, it wasn’t an Evil Gecko.

It was still a pitch-black quadrupedal creature, but the details were slightly different.

Evil Newt  

LV35  

\<Miasma Proliferation LV2>  

Notes: An amphibian monster that operates within miasma and gradually expands the area of miasma.

“The gecko turned into a newt…”

It’s also a bit stronger.

…I have no idea what this means.

“The feel of defeating it isn’t much different.”

“Do reptilian-type and amphibian-type classifications really make a difference for monsters…?”

Sakura tilts her head.

They’re monsters, so biological classification might not mean much.

This world is pretty sloppy about that sort of thing…

“Sakura-sama, newts are amphibians, so their primary habitat is around water. Could there be a water source somewhere in the mine?”

Unexpected. Mio knew about newts.

I see. Habitat classification might actually have meaning.

From that point on, the appearance rate of Evil Geckos gradually decreased, while the appearance rate of Evil Newts increased.

…This is really confusing.

After walking for a while, we finally discovered what seemed to be the cause.

As an aside, even though it wasn’t a single path and I hadn’t looked ahead on the map, we reached it in one go.

“I thought the miasma was gradually getting thicker, but this is awful.”

We emerged into an open space, and the first thing that caught my eye was a spring of miasma.

A nearly 50-meter-wide black spring. What filled it wasn’t water, but miasma.

As mentioned earlier, miasma is black smoke.

But just as gas can condense into liquid, it seems miasma can also become liquid.

Naturally, the concentration is higher, and the negative effects are likely stronger.

“A water source, but it’s a miasma water source… There’s no way even the military could handle this.”

“Even elite soldiers wouldn’t get away unscathed if they touched miasma at this concentration.”

“I think it would be difficult without my barrier or extremely high-level resistance.”

Even so, Maria’s \<Barrier Arts> can block it. Incredibly excellent.

Indeed, this is something even the nation couldn’t deal with.

Abandon it and leave it as an abandoned mine. That makes sense.

Incidentally, this abandoned mine wasn’t off-limits. Locals wouldn’t approach it, and even if outsiders entered, no one would really be inconvenienced.

Miasma was also drifting around the outside of the mine, so outsiders probably wouldn’t want to enter anyway…

Thinking that far, I had a realization.

“Ah, I see. The reason there were no Evil Geckos around the outside of the abandoned mine might be because the military deals with those that come out. Maybe they didn’t go inside, but they were still handling the situation?”

“Hm. Perhaps Carmine’s unit exterminated them.”

The city closest to this abandoned mine is the ‘Ochiba City’.

It’s possible that Carmine was handling the area around the mine.

A: Carmine’s unit was purifying the miasma in the City of Withered Leaves, so I believe that is correct.

Alta reinforced the hypothesis.

Incidentally, purifying miasma is the job of Recovery Magic. As you can tell from the fact that Poison Resistance can block it, it’s basically treated the same as poison.

This is a bit late to mention, but Carmine had fairly high Poison Resistance. A royal who needs Poison Resistance…

“So, Aunt Rouge beat up Carmine, who was exposing herself to miasma to defeat monsters for the sake of the citizens, in a place where the citizens couldn’t see.”

“That’s a very misleading way to put it… And don’t call me aunt.”

Rouge makes a very, very displeased face.

“If she was tired, she could have rested in the city. Why would she go out of her way to come outside the city just to provoke me?”

“Carmine-sama has always been like that, hasn’t she?”

According to Minerva, even if it meant pushing herself, Carmine has always gone out of her way to look down on Rouge.

She’s normal with her other siblings and relatives, but she apparently has an intense dislike for Rouge alone.

“What did I ever do to her…?”

It’s possible you did something without realizing it. It’s Rouge, after all.

While we were chatting leisurely a little distance away from the miasma spring, I suddenly felt something off.

“What is it?”

A: Master. A large number of monsters are about to emerge from the miasma spring.

The next moment, a large number of monsters erupted from the miasma spring.

More precisely, as follows:

Evil Gecko x48  

Evil Newt x59

“I can’t tell them apart!”

Looking at the two types of monsters, both pitch-black quadrupedal creatures wriggling around, I feel overwhelmed by a sense of helplessness.

If it were Asai, he probably could have distinguished them without difficulty…

“I don’t think it matters for defeating them…”

Mio says exasperatedly.

That’s true, but it still feels frustrating.

“So, Master. Since it’s such a large group of monsters, could you let Mio-chan handle it once in a while?”

“Yeah, sure.”

“Yes! Then I’ll take you up on that…”

Saying that, Mio pours magical power into the Comet Bow, draws the string, and releases.

Arrows made of magical power are fired all at once, automatically homing in on and piercing over a hundred freshly born Evil whatevers.

“No sense of accomplishment at all.”

“I know.”

“Right?”

As is common for long-range attackers, when there’s such a big difference in strength, you don’t really feel like you fought.

Well, it seems El, who was using close-range attacks, feels the same way…

“So monsters spawn in large numbers like that here.”

Rouge mutters thoughtfully.

“Something wrong?”

“No, it just seems impossible to deal with this, no matter how you think about it…”

“Normally speaking, that would be true.”

With a high-concentration miasma spring that’s nearly impossible to touch and difficult even to approach, and on top of that, the possibility of large-scale monster outbreaks, it wouldn’t be an exaggeration to say it’s impossible to deal with (in general terms).

“Jin-sama, could you do something about it? As a member of the Imperial family of this country, I would prefer not to leave such a dangerous place unattended if possible.”

“If you’re asking whether I can or can’t, I probably can.”

Just off the top of my head, I can think of more than a handful of methods.

“Then I ask you. I know that, as a slave, using one’s master like this would normally be unforgivable, but…”

“It’s fine.”

“Eh? It is…?”

Rouge looks more surprised than anything at my easy acceptance.

“After coming all this way, leaving without doing anything would be ridiculous, wouldn’t it?”

If I were acting as an adventurer, that would be one thing, but this is sightseeing, and I came expecting events.

If it’s something rare and better off eliminated, there’s no option not to eliminate it.

Incidentally, when I’m acting as an adventurer, I prioritize adventurer protocol over my own preferences.

Acting only has meaning when you do it seriously.

“I-I see… Then I’ll leave it to you.”

“Yeah, leave it to me.”

Alta, just to confirm, it’s okay to erase that thing, right?

A: Yes. There would be no harm in erasing it.

Alright then. Now, how should I make the miasma spring disappear?

The easiest way would be to just “throw it into \<Infinite Storage>”, but that feels way too lacking in atmosphere.

-Gogogogogo-

While I was thinking that, the miasma spring began to tremble.

“Is another massive monster outbreak coming!?”

“No, it seems a little different.”

The miasma spring gradually changes shape.

This isn’t what Rouge called a “massive monster spawn”.

If anything, this is “the spiritization of miasma”.

Magical power is not originally life.

However, it can gain will and become a spirit, and spirits can also absorb miasma.

Magical power, miasma, and spirits are all quite closely related existences.

In that case, it wouldn’t be strange for miasma itself to become a spirit.

A: This is an abnormal situation.

It seems it was strange after all.

After a while, the miasma spring disappeared, and a single spirit (or something like one) appeared.

“Black… Rain?”

The miasma spirit looked like my contracted spirit Rain, but turned black.

Its entire body was black, beyond dark brown to pitch black. It had a female form, was naturally completely naked, and its height and proportions were very similar to Rain’s, with an artistic, beautiful… yet ominous presence.

Its hair was also long, extending beyond its height, just like Rain’s.

Perhaps because it was just born, its consciousness wasn’t yet clear, and it looked spaced out.

A: If we do not consider the difference between miasma and magical power, the miasma spring was in a state where it would not be strange for a spirit to be born. And when the spirit came into being here, the miasma changed in a directional way. Since Rain was used as a reference, the appearance also came to resemble Rain.

So basically, Rain’s second palette color.

“…”

Speak of the devil, and Rain popped out.

“What is it?”

When I asked, Rain made a thoughtful gesture, then pointed at the miasma spirit and appealed to me.

“She wants me to leave dealing with that to her?”

Rain nods repeatedly.

“Got it. I’ll leave it to you.”

Rain nods strongly, her face filled with motivation.

“Master, you can really understand what she wants with just that…”

“It’s probably because we’re contracted. I can kind of tell what she’s trying to say.”

Rain doesn’t speak. She probably can, but chooses not to.

Even so, I can generally understand what she wants to say, so it hasn’t been a problem.

Rain floats over to the miasma spirit (I’ll call it a miasma spirit for now, since it’s a hassle).

We’ll decide the miasma spirit’s official name later with Mio.

-Pit-

-Bikun!-

-Purun!-

When Rain touches the spaced-out miasma spirit, the miasma spirit arches back dramatically.

Its well-shaped chest jiggles.

Rain continues touching the miasma spirit in silence for a while.

The miasma spirit remains passive, occasionally twitching and jiggling.

“What is she doing?”

“No idea.”

Mio asks curiously, but I don’t know either.

A: She is giving her own magical power to the miasma spirit. The miasma spirit was just born and had a weak sense of self. By giving it magical power that is a part of Rain, she is bringing the miasma spirit’s nature closer to her own.

What will the end result be?

A: Simply put, she is making the miasma spirit an ally. It is likely she will desire a spirit contract with the miasma spirit.

While I was listening to Alta’s explanation, Rain finished and led the miasma spirit by the hand as they approached.

The miasma spirit was wearing a black cloak, matching Rain’s but in a different color, and flew through the air with similar semi-transparent black wings.

In its deep, pitch-black eyes, there was now a clear intelligence that hadn’t been there before.

“…!”

“I see. You want to make this child one of ours, huh…”

To Rain, this miasma spirit would become something like a younger sister.

Its nature is a bit different from ordinary spirits, but Rain herself is already an outlier among spirits, so it’s not something to worry about now.

“Alright. But if we’re going to contract her…”

Before I could finish, the miasma spirit sent over the formation used for \<Spirit Arts>.

“A Great Spirit” requests a spirit contract. Do you permit it? Y/N

Like Rain, the miasma spirit desired a spirit contract of its own accord.

In this case, it’s normally an unfavorable contract for the spirit, so it’s apparently not something that usually happens…

“Are you really okay with this?”

-Nod.-

Her resolve seems firm, so I accepted the contract with the miasma spirit.

You have formed a spirit contract (master) with “Great Spirit.”

Would you like to name the “Great Spirit”?

I saw this earlier too, but miasma spirits are treated as Great Spirits.

“The name is…”

-Nod.-

She wants a name.

Name her “Eclipse”

Name her “Lake”

Name her “Yukari”

“Then your name is Eclipse.”

Like Rain, it’s a name inspired by the color of her eyes.

Those deep, dark eyes that feel like they could suck you in made me think of an eclipse.

Incidentally, “Lake” was taken from the miasma spring, or rather, lake, while matching Rain phonetically. Considering its formation, lake fits better than spring…

When I named her, Eclipse broke into a bright smile.

Just as intended, it was a smile very much like Rain’s.

“And now, about the ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’…”

To reduce spirit consumption, a mineral called a ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’ is necessary.

Do I still have one worthy of a Great Spirit?

“…!”

“Huh, you don’t need one? Like Rain, you’ll go into the ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’ I absorbed?”

Rain’s ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’ was absorbed by me using \<Life and Death Authority>.

As a result, I myself serve as Rain’s dedicated Spirit Brilliance Stone.

But can two spirits inhabit a single ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’?

And can a new spirit be added to an already absorbed ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’?

A: Normally, both would be impossible, but because their natures have been aligned to this extent and they share the same master, it has become possible as an exception.

If Alta says it can be done, then it probably can.

I touch Eclipse and try putting her into the ‘Spirit Brilliance Stone’.

She goes in.

I take her out.

“No problems so far. What about both at the same time?”

-Both go in.-

-Both come out.-

“No problems there either. Then, I look forward to working with you.”

-Nod.-

Thus, I formed a spirit contract with a new Great Spirit who governs miasma, Eclipse.

And she doesn’t talk either…

Ah, here are her stats.

Name: Eclipse  

LV1  

Gender: Female  

Age: 0  

Race: Great Spirit  

Skills: \<Spirit LV > \<Miasma Control LV >  

Notes: A Great Spirit who governs miasma.

\<Miasma Control> apparently lets her do pretty much anything, like absorbing, releasing, dispersing, and altering miasma.

Rain governs spirits and magical power, and Eclipse governs miasma. They really are sisters.

“So, Rouge, I took care of it.”

“This isn’t how I imagined it being handled, but it seems it worked out. The miasma is gone, and it even feels like the air is clearer. Thank you. Truly.”

Since the miasma spring became Eclipse, it has already disappeared.

Eclipse can freely choose whether to emit miasma or not. Right now, she’s refraining from releasing miasma out of consideration for the surroundings.

As a result, the area where the miasma spring once was now has less miasma than ordinary land.

“I’m satisfied too. We got a new spirit companion, and abandoned mines really are treasure troves of events.”

“Well, now that the miasma spring is gone, this mine will probably be used as tunnels again.”

“Oh, right… So it won’t be an abandoned mine anymore…”

My mood drops sharply.

So it’s no longer an abandoned mine…

“Eh, Master, that’s what makes your mood drop!?”

Mio looks shocked, but I have no use for tunnels that aren’t abandoned mines.

“Let’s go home.”

**AN:** Whether it’s magical power or miasma, if it’s in the form of a girl, I can love it.
